<div id="review_1257088930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257088930" />
    <a title="Tanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya"><img alt="Tanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602837639p2/15698555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257088930?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya">Tanya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200227" href="/book/show/20493986-interesting-times">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257088930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7090495605909474941"><b>Mighty Battles! Revolution! Death! War! (and his sons Terror and Panic, and daughter Clancy)!</b><br/><br/>I have a really hard time reviewing Discworld books, so this will be short. Once I'm through reading them chronologically, I think I'll start over and go by sub-series, because I'm clearly having trouble remembering characters from one sub-series-book to the next (I spent a good chunk of the book thinking "who the fuck is Twoflower?").<br/><br/>The Rincewind novels are without a doubt my least favorite—he's just n</span>
  <span id="freeText7090495605909474941" style="display:none"><b>Mighty Battles! Revolution! Death! War! (and his sons Terror and Panic, and daughter Clancy)!</b><br /><br />I have a really hard time reviewing Discworld books, so this will be short. Once I'm through reading them chronologically, I think I'll start over and go by sub-series, because I'm clearly having trouble remembering characters from one sub-series-book to the next (I spent a good chunk of the book thinking "who the fuck is Twoflower?").<br /><br />The Rincewind novels are without a doubt my least favorite—he's just not an engaging protagonist. Everything that happens to him, happens passively and as an accident / result of his bad luck; he spends every single book trying to get away from the action. Which would be entertaining if he were a secondary character, but is mostly kinda infuriating because he isn't. His books are also the ones where the shitty Pratchett jokes usually come forth (i.e. the mildly racist/sexist and rapey ones). There was one in particular in this one that really made me cringe. Why, Terry?<br /><br />With that said, this was overall one of the more enjoyable Rincewind novels, where I actually didn't mind his aversion to adventure at all—mainly because it was juxtaposed to Cohen and his elderly Barbarian Horde. I really enjoyed the socio-political aspects of this one as well, but found it a bit disjointed. The Luggage, for instance: it was clear that he didn't have a place for it in the main narrative, but couldn't just leave it out, so came up with a tiny, silly sub-plot. Then again, there were some jokes that made me laugh out loud to the point that I had to put the book down (the pig Latin spell and the bit about oral sex come to mind).<br /><br />—————<br /><br /><i>All my book reviews can be found <a href="https://watercolorstain.wordpress.com/reviews-by-title/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> · Buy on <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Interesting-Times-Terry-Pratchett/9781473200227?a_aid=watercolorstain" rel="nofollow noopener">BookDepository</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7090495605909474941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1778212632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1778212632" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1778212632?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778212632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6749937853808902055"><i>Interesting Times</i> is from the <i>Rincewind</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. It’s been quite a few books since I’ve seen Rincewind, so it was fun to see him again. He always makes me laugh. <br/><br/>If you’ve read the earlier books, you may remember that Rincewind once had some adventures with Twoflower, a visitor from the Counterweight continent. In this book Rincewind finds himself, quite against his will of course, dropping in on the Counterweight continent and getting caught up in a revolution. <br/><br/>It was a lot of fu</span>
  <span id="freeText6749937853808902055" style="display:none"><i>Interesting Times</i> is from the <i>Rincewind</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. It’s been quite a few books since I’ve seen Rincewind, so it was fun to see him again. He always makes me laugh. <br /><br />If you’ve read the earlier books, you may remember that Rincewind once had some adventures with Twoflower, a visitor from the Counterweight continent. In this book Rincewind finds himself, quite against his will of course, dropping in on the Counterweight continent and getting caught up in a revolution. <br /><br />It was a lot of fun seeing Twoflower again, although we didn’t see as much of him as I would have liked. Cohen the Barbarian, an elderly hero, also shows up in this book along with his “horde” which consists of a bunch of other elderly barbarian heroes plus a former school teacher. I thought the horde was really funny. The book alternates, for the most part, between the stuff happening with Rincewind and the stuff happening with the horde. <br /><br />There were some really funny parts in this book. October is full of business travel for me, and I was sitting in a hotel room trying very hard to stifle my laughter while reading the section where Rincewind tries to read a story written with pictograms [urinating dog, urinating dog]. It just got funnier the longer it went on. The story itself was ok. I didn’t think it wasn’t anything special, but the humor made up for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6749937853808902055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elowen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elowen" href="/user/show/71797035-elowen">Elowen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12576439334628606077">I'm sad to say this is the first Discworld novel I did not finish. Rincewind and Cohen aren't my favourite characters to begin with, but the plot itself is very thin too. Nothing much happened in the first half of the book. Rincewind gets sent to this largely unknown continent where he meets Cohen and a few locals who are getting ready for a rebellion. The Luggage is in there but I have no idea why. Every character just seems to wander around for no real reason. <br/><br/>The "unknown continent" itself is</span>
  <span id="freeText12576439334628606077" style="display:none">I'm sad to say this is the first Discworld novel I did not finish. Rincewind and Cohen aren't my favourite characters to begin with, but the plot itself is very thin too. Nothing much happened in the first half of the book. Rincewind gets sent to this largely unknown continent where he meets Cohen and a few locals who are getting ready for a rebellion. The Luggage is in there but I have no idea why. Every character just seems to wander around for no real reason. <br /><br />The "unknown continent" itself is a mixture of Japanese and Chinese cultural elements, but is closer to being offensive than funny, with the complete absence of Pratchett's sharp and witty social commentary. Maybe this book just didn't age well, maybe it was never that funny to begin with. Just give me Granny Weatherwax already. Those wizards are boring.</span>

<div id="review_2581907134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581907134" />
    <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo"><img alt="Alfred Haplo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599680519p2/34550725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581907134?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alfred Haplo" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo">Alfred Haplo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6567845-interesting-times">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=sf-fantasy-mytho">sf-fantasy-mytho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=fun-haha">fun-haha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581907134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14794596019282027314"><i>Interesting Times</i> is my best Rincewind book to-date *, which is bizarre to contemplate. In recalling my past impressions of Rincewind’s character, something struck me at once. I no longer feel irked but indifferent by DiscWorld’s resident irritant and craven wizard, now relegated to necessary evil status. His is a character so entrenched with fans that changing anything about his personality might result in revolt. Instead, his surroundings are changed around him, with best wishes to everyone el</span>
  <span id="freeText14794596019282027314" style="display:none"><i>Interesting Times</i> is my best Rincewind book to-date *, which is bizarre to contemplate. In recalling my past impressions of Rincewind’s character, something struck me at once. I no longer feel irked but indifferent by DiscWorld’s resident irritant and craven wizard, now relegated to necessary evil status. His is a character so entrenched with fans that changing anything about his personality might result in revolt. Instead, his surroundings are changed around him, with best wishes to everyone else. If I can accept the character, I can rationalize my feelings about the story. <br /><br />Fortunately, accidental hero is a mantle Rincewind wears well, particularly if the alternative is either bad or worse. Besides, every other main character is far better developed but those would have to be killed, or maimed, or made to suffer, or at the very least, philosophized, and must therefore not be wasted in <i>Interesting Times</i>. So, Rincewind it is, and Rincewind is teleported as sacrificial emissary to the cultural and economic backwater on the far side of the Disc, the Counterweight Continent. <br /><br />Welcome to China? Where else would exist a Great Wall, Forbidden City, The Art of War, Sum Dim (the purpose of this reversal escapes me), summer palace, women with small feet, and a red clay army? Not to be confused with the other country of the ninjas, kimonos and sumo wrestlers variety, which is also lumped into the dynastic Agatean Empire. To be fair, other countries assert their positions here for joke material as well, but none bears the brunt as much as the Chinese. When distinct Asian cultures are melded into a generic “Aurientals”, and comedy is made at their expense without reciprocity, I feel indignant on their behalf but indulged in silly laughing anyway. A readymade template of stereotypes plugged in with Rincewind is designed to be lighthearted, so why fight it. <br /><br />Even if that bit of sensitivity can be overcome, there is the Silver Horde. Cohen and his ancient bro-barbarians are here to pillage the Agatean Empire. When a group of white, albeit comical, foreigners invade an Asian-like continent, with talks of rape and rapine, and all the while the local citizenry is portrayed as ignoramus and simpletons, and are immediately subservient to ruling change, it sits rather uncomfortably. <br /><br />There is a distinct social hierarchy within the Agatean people - the peasants, the rebels, the learned, the rulers - but here, they are presented as a monolith. The whole of Agatean is just A Caricature, the “other” people. The people who speak funny, are named funny, work funny, obey funny, rule funny because they are not like “us". Which is oddly going against the grain, coming from Pratchett, this heavy-handed humor.<br /><br />I feel sorry for the missed opportunities. The Agateans are viewed from a skewed outsider perspective but more interesting would be from within their own in the manner of the excellent <i>Pyramids</i>. Two new refreshing characters, Mr Saveloy, teacher turned barbarian-diplomat, and Pretty Butterfly, skeptical young rebel, looked promising for bridging the cultural divide but both are under-utilized. Introspection is ironically focused on the foreign invaders and not the invaded, in how they deal with aging, mortality, and following one’s true calling. It is easy to be drawn into the emotional aspects of that, until you realized that the Silver Horde is just a bunch of killers who never grew up. <br /><br /><i>Interesting Times</i> is a peculiar sort of novel that is neither here nor there, where everyone and everything is sort of out of place. Except Rincewind, of course, who is exactly where he should be down under... Down under what? Down under my stack of DiscWorld books, 17 and counting.<br /><br /><br />[* Rincewind sub-series: <i>The Color or Magic</i> Discworld #1, Rincewind #1, <i>Light Fantastic</i> DW #2, RW #2, <i>Sourcery</i> DW #5, RW #3, <i>Eric <s>Faust</s></i> DW #9, RW #4]</span>
  <a data-text-id="14794596019282027314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2352632457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352632457" />
    <a title="writegeist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5052871-writegeist"><img alt="writegeist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304532745p2/5052871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352632457?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="writegeist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="writegeist" href="/user/show/5052871-writegeist">writegeist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200227" href="/book/show/20493986-interesting-times">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352632457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13930309591123513867">I'm torn when it comes to Rincewind. His introduction in the first two Discworld novels were not my favorites... but... there is always such a wealth of characters swirling around in a Discworld novel that you're never bored. The Horde, the geriatric barbarians lead by Cohen the Barbarian, are a kick. Several old friends show up as well. However, the more I think about the <em>wizzard</em>, I wonder if my problem with Rincewind has more to do with the fact that I see myself in him? I'm pretty sure I'd be</span>
  <span id="freeText13930309591123513867" style="display:none">I'm torn when it comes to Rincewind. His introduction in the first two Discworld novels were not my favorites... but... there is always such a wealth of characters swirling around in a Discworld novel that you're never bored. The Horde, the geriatric barbarians lead by Cohen the Barbarian, are a kick. Several old friends show up as well. However, the more I think about the <em>wizzard</em>, I wonder if my problem with Rincewind has more to do with the fact that I see myself in him? I'm pretty sure I'd be just as resolved to the hopelessness of the situation (I have been known to panic as my first response to a crisis; ask my wife!). Maybe I'm irritated because I see myself in him. Thanks, Sir Terry. I get it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13930309591123513867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_901168929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/901168929" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10227292-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339713181p2/10227292.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/10227292-jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901168929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16137360089479406444">Yay for seeing Twoflower again! And any story with Cohen tends to be funny. I wish Lord Hong had been less one-dimensional though: his whole character revolved around "I can do everything better than everyone else." That gets boring very quickly. I would have loved to see him interact with Vetinari, since he held him in such high regard.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_39925134'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39925134-missing-wings"><img alt="Missing Wings: Chronicles of the Aranysargas (Aranysargas, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1524456459l/39925134._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G4EDVaW0m2HKLX92tm/u3mTg0FQhoK4Xx9+ib4lBXUVOxpTzk28mI+W0z59mDRSqXYA0lrgMjNx5Wuk8ZK/TgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3447906813777641839">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText3447906813777641839" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
